KOREA
SECOND INDUSTRIAL FINANCE PROJECT
Korea Long-Term Credit Bank
Statement of Investment and Operational Policies
Approved at the Board of Directors' Meeting; April 25, 1967
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; February 29, 1968
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; February 26, 1973
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; February 26, 1974
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; December 17, 1974
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; June 19, 1975
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; July 23, 1976
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; June 11, 1977
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; January 31, 1979
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; December 15, 1981
Amended at the Board of Directors' Meeting; October 25, 1983
Korea Long Term Credit Bank (KLB), whose object is to promote the
expansion of private enterprise in the Republic of Korea, will be guided by
the policies set forth below:
I.   The Scope of Investment Activities
(1)  KLB will invest in productive enterprises.  While its primary
investment activity will be in manufacturing and processing indus-
tries, it may invest also in other types of enterprises, including
transport, tourism, and -ommercially-oriented agriculture.
(2)  KLB will finance private enterprises which are properly organized
and managed. KLB will not, in principle, invest in undertakings
which are Government-owned and operated, but a Government holding of
not more than 50% of the voting stock of a private enterprise shall
not make such enterprise ineligible for financial assistance from
KLB. KLB will finance both new enterprises and existing ones for
expansion or improvement.
(3)  In its operations, KLB will give due regard to the Government's
general economic plans and policies. The following categories of
industries will receive high priority, in accordance with the
Government's economic policies and objectives:
(a) Export and import-substitute industries;
(b) Industries contributing to the deepening of industrial
structure;



-82 -                        ANNEX 3
Attachment 1
Page 2 of 4
(c) Industries which contribute to balanced regional development,
and have greater potential for employment creation;
(d) Natural resource development industries, domestic as well as
foreign; and
(e) Industries promoting international economic cooperation.
(4)  KLB will assist private enterprises in the following ways:
(a) Medium and long-term loans;
(b) Equity participation (through underwriting, conversion rights,
direct participation in share capital or otherwise);
(c) Guarantee of payment for machinery and equipment imported or
otherwise;
Cd) Guarantee and underwriting of corporate securities;
(e)  Technical, managerial and other financial advice and services;
(f)  Foreign exchange operations; and
(g) Any other appropriate manner.
(5)  KLB will seek through its operation to broaden the ownership of
private securities in Korea;
(6)  KLB's financial assistance will be primarily for expenditures for
fixed assets. KLB will also extend working capital loans to
enterprises;
(7)  KLB will study periodically the trend of overall industrial
development and investment opportunities in the private sector in
cooperation with research institutes for promotion of new enter-
prises or expansion of the existing ones.
II. Basis for Investment Decisions
(8)  KLB will make investment decisions only on the basis of sound
investment criteria and standards, and will provide financial
assistance only to those projects which are financially and econ-
omically sound and technically feasible. Special attention will be
given to the ability of management and the profitability of the
enterprise.
(9) KLB will ensure that the funds provided to the enterprises are
properly used in accordance with the purpose of such financing. KLB
will require its borrower, if it is deemed necessary, to purchase
the equipments through international competitive bidding or other
appropriate method when such equipment is procured with the proceeds
of an official loan.



-83 -                           ANEX 3
Attachment 1
Page 3 of 4
III. Diversification of Portfolio
(10) KLB will diversify its portfolio in order to maintain a reasonable
level of risk;
(11) KLB wiLl not provide financial assistance of less than the equiva-
lent of $50,000 for the purpose of capital expenditure. The maxiunm
financial commitment in whatever form, including loan, share capital
or guarantee or any combination thereof, that KLB may make to any
single enterprise will not normally exceed 25% of the total of KLB's
paid-in capital and free reserves.
(12)  KLB wiLl not commit to any single enterprise in any form of share
capital more than 1OZ of KLB's paid-in capital and free reserves.
The aggregate equity investment of [LB at any time will not exceed
the total of its paid-in share capital and free reserves.
(13) In undertaking large-size projects, KLa will seek cooperation with
other financial institutions, both domestic and foreign.
IV. Turn-Over of Portfolio
(14) In order to recover its resources for new commitments and to encour-
age widespread ownership of private securities, KLB will revolve its
portfolio whenver it can do so on satisfactory terms. In selling an
investment it will pay due regard not only to its own interest but
also to the interest of other participants in such investments, as
also to the interest of the concern whose shares are involved.
V.  Relationship with Enterprises Financed
(15) Normally, KLB will not take a controlling interest in any enterprise
in which it has invested, or other interest which would give it
primary responsibility for management and it also will not acquire
more than 252 of the share capital of an enterprise.
(6)  In accordance with normal banking practice, [LB will require its
borrowers to provide and to maintain adequate security, to keep
records and accounts in accordance with sound accounting practices,
and to furnish whatever information on their operations and accounts
KLB deems desirable.  KLB will take the right to inspect the enter-
prises it finances as well as their operations and accounts.
(17) Business secrets and other information furnished by applicants or
clients will be treated as confidential.
VI. Financial Guidelines
(18) KLB will lend and invest its resources in such a way as to maintain
the value of its capital. [RLB will pass to its clients any foreigr.
exchange risk it assumes or find other suitable means to cover it.



ANNEX 3
- 84 -                        Attachment 1
Page 4 of 4
(19)  KLB will not incur any debt (maturing more than one year after date
of original incurrence) in excess of 12 times the aggregate of its
paid-in capital and free reserves.
(20)  KLB will maintain accounting records adequate to reflect its
business operations in accordance with sound and generally accepted
international accounting practices and standards. KLB will employ
qualified and independent public accountants to audit its books and
certify the accounts annually.
VII. Profits and Their Distribution
(21)  KLB will seek to develop earnings sufficient to cover expenses and
taxes, to provide reserves adequate to the size and risks of its
portfolio and to protect its equity against erosion and to pay
satisfactory dividends. It will seek profits on its equity invest-
ments and will impose interest rates, fees and other charges for its
loans and services which wilL permit it to achieve that level of
profitability. It will build and maintain reserves consistent with
sound financial management. It will set aside each year from net
income before tax the amount required by law as the legal reserve.
In addition, it will accumulate other reserves, including reserve
for losses, as considered prudent by the Board of Directors.
VIII. Staff
(22) KLB will build up a technically qualified staff capable of carrying
the responsibilities which KLB's objectives create, and able to
provide the services to clients which those objectives call for.
IX. Revision of Policies
(23)  Any proposal to revise this Statement of Investment and Operational
Policies shall be considered by the Board of Directors only after
each member has been given an adequate opportunity to study and
comment on the proposal, and it shall be approved at a meeting of
the Board of Directors by two-thirds of all directors.

KOREA
SECOND INDUSTRIAL FINANCE PROJECT
Korea Long-Term Credit Bank
Development Strategy 1985-1986
Amidst the transition toward a reform aimed at liberalization,
Korea's financial sector is expected to face further competition in the years
ahead. Such competition, as triggered by the Government's privatization of
coamercial banks, is being enhanced by the recent move taken by the Government
t'jward greater autonomy in bank management, adjustment of the scope of busi-
ness among financial institutions, and gradual opening of domestic financial
market to international financing institutions. Under the circumstances.
KLB's Development Strategy for 1985-86 is focused on the expansion and diver-
sification of financial services so as to make its way under the increasingly
competitive environment.
Expansion and Diversification of Financial Services
(a) Expansion of Business Scope. The Bank will continue its efforts to
expand its scope of business so that it can provide diversified
financi.1 services to its clients. Also, the Bank will endeavor to
sophisticate its services through enhanced operational efficiency as
well as through expanded public relations activities.
(b) Expansion of the Bales for Resource Mobilization. The Bank will
continue to develop new financial instruments and enhance debenture
sales promotion activities, so as to expand its bases for resource
mobilization. In this connection, the Bank plans to develop new
debentures including those with longer maturities and to introduce
debenture sales promotion agent, who will be selected from those of
high moral influence and will specialize in promotion of debenturc.
sales through close liaison between KLB and prospective debenture
sales through close liaison between KLB and prospective debenture
clients. The Bank will also endeavor to strengthen its branch net-
work, for which it plans to add a subbranch in 1985.
(c) Reinforcement of Davelopmental Role. As the first and soLe private
development bank, 'B will continue to reinforce its developmental
role by expanding strategic investments in private industries which
are conducive to depending of small and medium industries (SIs),
enhancing of international competitiveness, and technology develop-
ment. KLB will also endeavor to help develop industries of regional
areas through augment of regional clientele. Besides, KLB will con-
tinue to extend management consulting services including
computerization and internal control system to its clients,
especially to SHIs. Further, KLB will pursue to extend such
activities that are peripheral or related to financial services so
as to supplement its function.



ANNEX 3
- 86 -                       Attachment 2
Page 2 of 3
(d)  Expansion of Comprehensive Financial Services.  KLB will continue
its effort to provide integrated financial services both to its
debenture clients and to loan clients. Through expansion of the
integrated financial services, not only will KLB pursue more
efficient services to its clients but will better meet the diversi-
fying financial demands from its clients.
Organizational Development
(a)  Rearrangement of Organization.  In order to cope with the rapidly
changing financial environment, the Bank plans to rearrange its
organization to attain functional efficiency, through careful study
on each departmental role and function of its organization.
(b)  Computerization and Office Automation.  Along with its efforts for
computerization of operations, KLB will continue to promote estab-
lishment of the computerized MIS and Office Automation. In
addition, KLB will continue to establish a data base through
accumulation of financial information.   In this connection, KLB
will induce relevant advices and related techniques from external
sources, both domestic and international.
(c)  Enhancement of Productivity and Job Efficiency.  KLB will continue
to increase its productivity and job efficiency through various
efforts and movements such as job standardization, cost reduction,
study-group operations, TQC activities, aggressive-self-job-manage-
ment scheme, and performance-reflected pay system. Besides, KLB
will continue to strengthen its internal control system so that it
can provide efficient and flawless services to its clients.
(d)  Strengthening of Capital Base.  In order to expand its operational
capacity through strengthening of capital base, KLB will pay due
consideration to raising of its paid-in share capital. Basically,
[LB will pursue its strategy to build up its reserve   .a level
close to its paid-in share capital before issuing new shares, so as
to command a better price for the KLB shares.
(e)  Infusion of Bank-entrepreneurship.  Through systematic ttaining, KLB
will continue to develop its employees as specialized professional
bankers. During the course, KLB will infuse the spirit of bank-
entrepreneurship into each of its employees so that they can develop
owner-minded innovative attitude toward their jobs. [LB will also
emphasize on the training of its employees in strengthening their
personal role in selling the Bank's debentures loans and other
services, and in having their jobs done through negotiations,
cooperation and public relations.
Public Relations
(a) Seminars. KLB will continue to hold seminars with broad range of
subjects such as project financing, project feasibility analyses,



ANNEX 3
- 87 -                      Attachment 2
Page 3 of 3
MIS, internal :ontrol and so forth to assist the management of
business firms including its cLient companies. Also, it will
continue to have monthly discussion sessions with the executives of
its client companies for betterment of mutual understanding as well
as for exchange of business and financial information. Especially,
as for the SHIs, KLB will endeavor to identify and support the
sound and promising SMIs, and continue to hold sessions for intro-
duction of their companies as well as their products to other
interested client companies.
(b) Operation of Center for Economic and Business Education. KLB will
continue to strengthen operation of its Center for Economic and
Business Education, through which it will provide education on a
wide range of economic subjects and personal computers to general
public. RLB plans to expand such education to regional areas
through extension of classes to relevant regions.
Cc)  Research Activities.  In 1984, KLB successfully completed two public
research projects, one on the Prospect for a Socio-economic
Development of the Cheju Island Region and the other on the
Direction for Development of Industrial Structure in Daegu Region,
which provided references for the Government's setting up of long-
range plans for the regions. KLB, in cooperation with relevant
academic bodies, will continue to initiate such public research
projects in the future.
(d)  Promotion of Industrial Technology Development.  KLB plans to
establish a, namely, Industrial Technology Prize, which will be
conferred to some five nominees selected from its client companies
every year. The prize is aimed to honoring of technical staffs of
KLB's client companies who contributed substantially to technology
development in their companies, but relatively unnoticed elsewhere
for the performence. Such prize will conmmend those who constantly
pursue their duties in shady spots, so as to encourage their further
efforts.

KOREA
SECOND INDUSTRIAL FINANCE PROJECT
The Korea Development Bank
Policy Statement
Economic Role of KDB
1.        The KDB shall assist in the economic development of Korea in con-
formity with its purpose as stated in the Korea Development Bank Act (RDB Act)
enacted December 30, l953, as amended, its By-Laws enacted February 16, 1954,
as amended, and other other regulations governing its operations.
Operations
2.        The KDB will carry out its operations in accordance with sound
management and banking principles and practices. It shall endeavor to
specialize in extending capital funds to such industries as are designated by
the Government's economic plans or decrees as priority industries as well as
other major basic industries which form the substructure of the economy. KDB
may also make equity investments, provide working capital loans and render
managerial and technical assistance to its borrowers when the need arises.
KDB will also extend guarantees on behalf of client enterprises. KDB,
however, will not compete with other financial institutions in lending and
administering industrial loans to assist major industries.
Project Selection
3.        It will finance enterprises which are soundly managed and which
appear, on careful economic, financial and engineering investigation to be
viable. Following sound banking practices, the projects will be analyzed
taking the following factors into consideration before making a commitment of
financiaI assistance: (a) national economic benefits; (b) technical feasi-
bility; (c) financial soundness and profitability; (d) marketability; and
(e) quality of management.
Critria for Selection of Borrowers
4.        In its operations, preference will be given to the following major
industries:
(a) Generation, transmission and supply of electricity;
(b) Coal mining;
(c) Ship building;
(d) Iron and steel manufacturing;



ANNEX 4
- 125 -                         Attachment 1
Page 2
(e) Electronics;
(f) Export industries, designated by the Government to produce export
commodities;
(g) Import-substitution industries and industries producing raw
materials necessary for export and import-substitution;
(h)  Indigenous industries and labor-intensive industries; and
(i) Such other industries as may be designated by the Government's
economic plans or decrees as priority industries.
Qualifications for Eligible Borrowers
5.        Eligible borrowers for KDB financing must meet the following
qualifications:
(a) Borrowers must be financially sound;
(b) Borrowers must possess management and technical capacity for
implementing the projects being financed;
Cc) Borrowers should not have defaulted on any of their outstanding
obligations to KDB.
Maximum Investment and Assistance
6.   (a)  KDB shall not subscribe to and/or underwrite stocks (including
investment certificates) if the paid-up amount of the stocks so held
by KDB will exceed KDB's own paid-up capital;
(b)  KDB shall not normall, make equity investments in any single
enterprise in excess of either:
(i) fifteen percent (15X) of the total unimpaired paid-up captial,
surplus, and free reserves of KDB; or
(ii) fifty percent (50Z) of the paid in capital of the enterprise.
(c) KDB shall not normally extend financial assistance (loan, invest-
ments and guarantees) to any single enterprise which exceeds either
of the following ceilings:
(i) twenty-five percent (25Z) of KDB's total unimpaired paid-up
capital, surplus and free reserves;
(ii) sixty-five percent (65%) of the total assets of the enterprise.



ANNEX 4
- 126 -                        Attachment 1
Page 3
Foreign Exchange Risk
7.        As a general policy, KDB shall cover itself adequately against
foreign exchange risks in the conduct of its operations. However, in using
"revolving funds" generated in the case of some foreign borrowings, KDB may
assume the exchange risk temporarily.
Security Arrangements
8.   (a)  In accordance with normal business practices, KDB will obtain
adequate security for its loans and guarantees. In extending a loan
to an enterprise, KDB shall require such enterprise to provide
security the value of which shall be not less than 120% of the
amount of the Loan. In the case of guarantees covered by a
Government counter-guarantee the value of security shall be not less
than the amount guaranteed, an in all other cases of guarantees,
shall be not less than 120Z of the principal amount covered under
such guarantees.
(b) KDB may waive any of the foregoing requirements in cases where the
credit or the guarantee is extended in favor of those enterprises
enumerated in para. 2, Article 10 of the Operating Manuals of KDB as
of the date of this Policy Statement, provided however, that in such
cases KDB will endeavor to secure a guarantee or counter-guarantee
from the Government or from a suitabLe bank or banks to cover the
credit or guarantee granted.
Technical Assistance
9.        KDB will endeavor to provide its subborrowers with the necessary
technical services including assistance for upgrading production efficiency
and solving complicated technical difficulties. It will observe the opera-
tions of its subborrowers and will, whenever necessary, promptly make
available to them constructive and remedial advice on the operation of the
project. When considered necessary, KDB will also dispatch its own staff to
the project companies.
Management and Organization
10.       To build and strengthen its own management and staff as well as to
assist clients in the formulation and execution of their projects, KDB will
maintain an effective organization and an adequate staff, including financiaL
and economic analysis, engineering, accountancy, marketing and legal services.
Share-Holding Fund
11.       KDB shall administer the Share-holding Administration Fund (the
Fund) pursuant to the provisions of the KDB Share-holding Act (Act No. 2128,
enacted August 4, 1969) as a separate and distinct account in KDB's official
books, the Fund will be treated as segreated from the other transactions and
resources of RDB in accordance with the provisions of said Act.



- 127 -                          IANEX 4
Attachment 1
Page 4
Financial Policies
12.       KDB shall conduct its operations according to the provisions of the
KDB Act. It shall endeavor to match the maturity of its liabilities with
those of its assets. It will continually review the charges it levies for the
financial assistance it provides to ensure that it receives an adequate
"spread" to cover all its expenses including provisions for doubtful loans and
investments, and to enable it to build reserves as required legally and as
considered necessary by the management.



ANNEX 4
- 128 -                        Attachment 2
Page 1
KOREA
SECOND INDUSTRIAL FINANCE PROJECT
The Korea Development Bank
Outline of Development Strategy for 1985-90
1.        To achieve the goal of realizing an industriaLized society, the
Government will continue an export-oriented development strategy and emphasis
will be given to economic stabilization. Together with prudent aggregate
demand management, strong efforts will be made to encourage the public to join
the stabilization program. As an instrument of the Government's development
policy, KDB will in the six year period 1985-1990 further its development
activities particularly in the specific areas outlined below.
2. Project Promotion and Resources Allocation
(a) KDB will give priority financing for readjustment of the Industrial
structure by
i)  supporting the comparative advantageous industry sector and the
high value-added industry sector; and
(ii) expanding support areas such as the technological innovation
industry, the manpower developing industry, the energy-saving
industry, the anti-pollution industry, etc.
(b) KDB will increase its emphasis on financing the newly emerged
prospective industry projects, in particular, the high-tech
electronic industry, the new material industry, and genetic
engineering industry.
(c) KDB will expand its consultancy role to enterprises in the areas of
project formulation, project design, selection of technology,
engineering and project analysis, through further development of its
subsidiary companies - like KMCC and KTFC.
(d) KDB will continue to expand its contribution to the social overhead
capital sector to improve the people's standard of living through
the redevelopment of the biggest city and the modernization of
distribution facilities, prevention of pollution and improvement of
the environment, the expansion of waterworks and sewerage
facilities, railroads, roads, etc.
(e) KDB will endeavor to internationalize it banking operations by:
(i) enhancing the efficiency of the foreign capital inducement;



ANNEX 4
- 129 -                        Attachment 2
Page 2
(ii)  rationalizing the foreign-debt management system;
(iii)  upgrading of credit rating techniques through introduction of a
Loan-Officer System and improvement of feasibility research in
connection with project selection; and
(iv)  flexibly applying the security ratio according to the credit
ratings of the enterprises.
3.        Resource Mobilization.  In line with its objective of intensifying
its efforts at raising private resources, KDB plans to:
(a)  increase the issuing amount of domestic bonds (IFDs);
(b)  strengthen KDB's despoit-taking abilities; and
(c)  increase its authorized capital to Won 2.0 trillion by 1990.
4.        Return on Equity.  KDB will endeavor to realize a reasonable rate of
return on equity which would be sufficient to maintain the level of its equity
base in real terms.
5.        Return on Investments.  KDB will endeavour to increase the ratio of
return on investments to 2-3Z by 1990 by:
(a)  expanding development investment areas through increasing the
investment to the Venture Capital industry;
(b)  expediting the management rationalization of the invested
enterprise; and
Cc)  selling the capital stocks of the invested enterprises.
6.        Staff.
(a)  KDB will continue to enhance professional abilities of its staff
through adequate training courses (OJT, etc.) provided by domestic
and foreign institutions; and
(b)  To deal with the problem of data collection and processing on
personnel management, KDB will further develop computerization of
its banking operations.
7.   Organization.  KDB will endeavor to achieve its management goal by
(a) implementation of the responsibility management system; and
(b) elastic operation of the organization according to the change of the
management environment.
